  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_978a3036-417c-4b73-976e-6f502d771461'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();

      initializeSiwa();

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer11791502700749322412">The ever after, the demonic realm that parallels the human world, is shrinking. If it disappears completely, so does all magic. It's up to witch-turned-daywalking-demon Rachel Morgan to avert catastrophe and keep life from changing... for the worse.<br/><br/>While saving the world is important, it isn't Rachel's only motivation.   <span id="freeText11791502700749322412" style="display:none">The ever after, the demonic realm that parallels the human world, is shrinking. If it disappears completely, so does all magic. It's up to witch-turned-daywalking-demon Rachel Morgan to avert catastrophe and keep life from changing... for the worse.<br /><br />While saving the world is important, it isn't Rachel's only motivation. There's also the small fact that she caused the ley line to rip in the first place, setting off a chain reaction of unfortunate events. That little mistake has made her life forfeit unless she can fix it. It's also made her more than a few enemies, including the most powerful demon in the ever after—a terrifying entity who eats souls and now has an insatiable appetite for her. He's already kidnapped her friend and goddaughter to lure her out, and if Rachel doesn't give herself up soon, they'll die.<br /><br />But Rachel has more than a few impressive and frightening skills of her own, and she isn't going to hand over her soul and her life without one hell of a fight. She's also got a surprise: elven tycoon Trent Kalamack. With this unlikely ally beside her—a prospect both thrilling and unnerving—she's going to return to the ever after, kick some demon butt, rescue her loved ones... and prevent an apocalypse before it's too late. Or, at least that's the plan...</span>
  <a data-text-id="11791502700749322412" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/12236730-elise"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1345990664i/12236730._UY100_CR1,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>

<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/12236730-elise">Elise</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">There is character and relationship development that carries over from one book to the next so you will, for instance, find out that a character dies <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">There is character and relationship development that carries over from one book to the next so you will, for instance, find out that a character dies if you read them out of order but the stories themselves are pretty stand alone. She adds in enough of a summary of previous books that you wouldn't be super lost.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

<div id="review_282640716" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/282640716" />
    <a title="VampireNovelFan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4897902-vampirenovelfan"><img alt="VampireNovelFan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1296445543p2/4897902.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/282640716?book_show_action=true">Feb 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="VampireNovelFan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="VampireNovelFan" href="/user/show/4897902-vampirenovelfan">VampireNovelFan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4897902-vampirenovelfan?shelf=comedy">comedy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4897902-vampirenovelfan?shelf=elves">elves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4897902-vampirenovelfan?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4897902-vampirenovelfan?shelf=review-request">review-request</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4897902-vampirenovelfan?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4897902-vampirenovelfan?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4897902-vampirenovelfan?shelf=edelweiss">edelweiss</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4897902-vampirenovelfan?shelf=demons">demons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4897902-vampirenovelfan?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4897902-vampirenovelfan?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer282640716" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10126414222132614768"> <a href='http://vampirenovelfan.wordpress.com/2012/12/18/ever-after-like-the-finest-of-wines-the-hollows-gets-better-with-age/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <b>Like the finest of wines, The Hollows gets better with age!</b>
</a><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379780132i/401864._SY540_.jpg' width='402' height='714' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>As you can see, I present definitive proof that I've indeed read the book! And man oh man is it fantastic! It's my new favorite! I normally worry about using that term too loosely because it could diminish the potential quality of the series as a whole, but I genuinely think it's the best book thus far. Kim Harrison has done it yet again and all signs point to her doing it two more times, and in epic proportions.<br/><br/>This time the Ever </span>
  <span id="freeText10126414222132614768" style="display:none"> <a href="http://vampirenovelfan.wordpress.com/2012/12/18/ever-after-like-the-finest-of-wines-the-hollows-gets-better-with-age/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <b>Like the finest of wines, The Hollows gets better with age!</b>
</a><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379780132i/401864._SY540_.jpg" width="402" height="714" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>As you can see, I present definitive proof that I've indeed read the book! And man oh man is it fantastic! It's my new favorite! I normally worry about using that term too loosely because it could diminish the potential quality of the series as a whole, but I genuinely think it's the best book thus far. Kim Harrison has done it yet again and all signs point to her doing it two more times, and in epic proportions.<br><br>This time the Ever After, home of the demons, is shrinking at an alarmingly fast rate, placing the existence of magic in a pretty vulnerable position; without one there couldn't be the other. So as if our favorite itchy witch, Rachel Morgan, didn't have enough problems, this just sprang up to #1. If she can't solve this one, she won't have any others. If she can't fix it, the demons want her head as her botched leyline creation caused this mess in the first place. And no one wants to see that happen more than her old buddy, Ku'Sox, the former day walking demon who had the misfortune to cross Rachel and lose. He even resorts to abducting her friend and goddaughter as insurance...and boy is it effective. Thankfully she's got Trent Kalamack and Algaliarept by her side to restore balance and take him down once and for all. But the price may be too high for things to ever be the same again.<br><br>I know there was criticism about not a lot happening in A Perfect Blood, though I personally enjoyed the old-school Hollows style mystery. But for those of you who didn't, for EVER AFTER I think a better question is what *didn't* happen! There was so much going on that I genuinely can't recall a dull moment. I think I felt and continue to feel every emotion possible, but I ultimately finished the book in pure euphoria. In case you needed a little reminding, Harrison presents really harsh realities and difficult decisions that prove she's an author with guts. I don't think I've experienced so many pulse pounding moments since For a Few Demons More (book 5). This book left me reeling like no other.<br><br>The scenes that take place in the Ever-After were some of the best of the series. The race against the clock really made this book so intense. Learning the history of the demons and the elves and the eventual degradation of their relationship was great, though I would have loved even more insight. I just can't get enough of it.<br><br>And that brings me to Big Al, who was totally amazing. Fans will absolutely adore him in this book as we learn more about his personal back story. He's much more prominent here than in A Perfect Blood and that's fine by me because he literally lights up the pages and keeps things exciting in his own peculiar way.<br><br>After having read Trent's POV in the bonus chapter of A Perfect Blood, I saw everything he did in a whole new light, and boy was it refreshing. He's got his own personal demons to work through and it really makes you feel for the guy. He is in a rock and a hard place, accepting his actions that have led to certain consequences while still working to find the best solution possible. I loved seeing him use more magic. I feel like elves have a pretty powerful arsenal that deserve more exploration, so it was nice to see Harrison skim the surface here with the insinuation of even greater things. Magic is amped up for the elves, while more human qualities are amped up for the demons, so it was an interesting trade off.<br><br>His teamwork with Rachel was one of my favorite parts of the book. The tension was insane and placed so well all throughout. It's seriously amazing to go back and read passages from Dead Witch Walking and then look at them now. Their progress is usually one step forward, two steps back, but the slow burn for this ship is probably what will make it my all-time #1 favorite if they end up together *fingers crossed*.<br><br>This book was just about everything I could ask for, but it wasn't 100% flawless. With so much ever after, elf and demon action, the story manages to throw in a smidgeon of development in vampire politics. Unfortunately it felt very much like an afterthought and briefly broke the overall flow. We know vampires won't get a lot of focus until the final book 13, so 10 or so pages of development came off a random at best and forgettable at worst.<br><br>All in all, this is an absolute MUST READ for fans of the series. Since Black Magic Sanction and Pale Demon the series has been invigorated and manages to improve as we reach the final stretch. That is a rarity for 95% of series that make it this far. I think it helps a lot that Kim Harrison has an end in sight and continues to write towards that. Many others have jumped-the-shark by this point. The Hollows is absolutely revving up for a grande finale and I cannot wait to be there.<br><br>*ARC provided by the author (cuz she frickin' ROCKS!!)<br><br>*Review also posted to <a href="http://www.amazon.com/review/R10N9N9AXZ9HIB/ref=cm_cr_rdp_perm" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <b>Amazon</b>
</a>. <br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="10126414222132614768" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_514764260" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/514764260" />
    <a title="Ferdy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4596358-ferdy"><img alt="Ferdy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487898103p2/4596358.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/514764260?book_show_action=true">Jan 23, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ferdy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ferdy" href="/user/show/4596358-ferdy">Ferdy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/15853906-ever-after">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=abusive-love-interest">abusive-love-interest</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=awful-love-interest">awful-love-interest</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=wtf">wtf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=witchy-shit">witchy-shit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=fucked-up-romance">fucked-up-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=tstl-heroine">tstl-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=hero-dick-to-heroine">hero-dick-to-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=fucked-up-hero">fucked-up-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=doormat-heroine">doormat-heroine</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer514764260" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer908711391170071691"><b>Spoilers</b><br/><br/>Less a review and more a collection of ranty thoughts.<br/><br/>-Did Rachel really need to describe how good looking Trent was <i>every</i> single time she saw him? Also why was she so obsessed with how everyone smelt? <i>Ooh Trent smells like cinnamon, ooh Quen smells like cinnamon but a different kind of cinnamon'</i>. Enough with the pointless descriptions.<br/><br/>-Why was Rachel and Quen acting like Trent was a saint and some sort of speshul snowflake that would save all the elves? Trent has never been a good guy y</span>
  <span id="freeText908711391170071691" style="display:none"><b>Spoilers</b><br /><br />Less a review and more a collection of ranty thoughts.<br /><br />-Did Rachel really need to describe how good looking Trent was <i>every</i> single time she saw him? Also why was she so obsessed with how everyone smelt? <i>Ooh Trent smells like cinnamon, ooh Quen smells like cinnamon but a different kind of cinnamon'</i>. Enough with the pointless descriptions.<br /><br />-Why was Rachel and Quen acting like Trent was a saint and some sort of speshul snowflake that would save all the elves? Trent has never been a good guy yet Rachel and everyone else was constantly up his arse, bending over backwards for him, defending him and thinking he was a top notch guy. Ugh, I preferred it when Rachel didn't make excuses for Trent's vile behaviour.<br /><br />-Trent being affectionate towards Rachel was weird, creepy and cringey. Why was it so awkward?! I wanted heat and chemistry not awkwardness!<br /><br />-Ceri was a cow. Who did she think she was bitching about Rachel just because Rachel refused to protect Trent?! Rachel is a demon and a witch - Trent and the elves aren't Rachel's responsibility. Why Ceri acted like it was Rachel's duty to protect Trent… I don't know. Rachel didn't owe Ceri or Trent anything.<br /><br />-Why did Rachel feel responsible for everything and everyone. <i>'Oh, the ever after's shrinking and Al is hurting'</i> …It's all my fault. <i>'Oh Ceri and Lucy have been kidnapped'</i> …It's all my fault. <i>'Oh the vampires are evul and want to hurt Ivy and Nina'</i> …It's all my fault. <i>'Oh Bis has been taken'</i> …It's all my fault. <i>'Oh Trent is hurting'</i> …It's all my fault. <i>'Oh that thing happened to that dude'</i> …It's all my fault. SHUT THE FUCK UP RACHEL!! <br /><br />-Rachel's favourite word was 'sorry'. The thick cow kept apologising to everyone when she'd done nothing wrong. She was such a doormat. <br /><br />-Why did Rachel let everyone use, abuse and walk all over her?<br /><br />-I enjoyed Trent more when he was a ruthless businessman rather than a family man that kept worrying about Ceri and his daughters.<br /><br />-Rachel was too trusting especially in regard to Nick, Quen, the demons and Trent. She was a naive fool.<br /><br />-Rachel doing so much work (saving Trent, Lucy, the ever after, Quen) and not getting paid for it. WTF?!<br /> <br />-What was with all the bullshit with everyone feeling sorry for Trent because he apparently will always be alone and will have to give his life up for the greater elf good. He has a fucking life! He has two daughters, Quen, Ellasbeth and he'll always have Rachel being his bitch. Oh and he's also a billionaire. Yea… I don't feel sorry for him. He's got plenty.<br /><br />-Trent lying to Rachel and manipulating her <i>again</i>. Is Trent lying, using, abusing and manipulating Rachel supposed to be romantic? He obviously likes treating Rachel like shit.<br />Rachel just forgiving him straight away because she's a dumb bitch. <br /><br />-Trent said he wanted Rachel to be pure… so basically if she does something questionable he won't love/care/respect her anymore because she no longer deserves it or is worthy of it. Whilst Trent can go around being an evul drug lord, hunting people down, caging them up and killing anyone that gets in his way… and yet with all those despicable things under his belt he's still worthy of being loved.<br /><br />-Trent manipulates Rachel in to working for him for at least 20 years by threatening to kill a bunch of babies… Even though Trent wants to kill the babies, Rachel still thinks he's a decent guy. The reason he wanted to kill the babies? He was too lazy to use his billions of dollars to protect them. The dick head.<br /><br />-Trent's already got his HEA with Lucy. Rachel needs her own HEA. <br /><br />-Rachel deserves better than being Trent's bit on the side… he's going to get married to Ellasbeth and play happy families with her whilst Rachel won't ever get her own husband and kids. No, just no.<br />Rachel will never be a part of Trent's family — his real family will always be be Ray, Lucy, Quen and Ellasbeth. Rachel will always be the odd one out. She needs her own kids and family… and not just the scraps Trent deigns to throw at her.<br /><br />-Trent kept mementos of Rachel when they were in camp — that means he had feelings for her since they were children… yet those feelings didn't stop him putting her in cage when she turned into a ferret/rat thing or stop him from wanting to put her in a rat fight when she was a ferret/rat or stop him from hunting her down and killing her or stop him from choking her to death or stop him from repeatedly smashing her head against a headstone..he would have killed her if Ceri hadn't held him back… so it's obvious his feelings for her won't prevent him from hurting in the future. Watch out, Rachel… Trent will hurt/kill you if you do something he doesn't like.<br /><br />-Trent would never sacrifice anything for Rachel. Even when he lost his fingers to help Rachel in a previous book, he only did so because he knew Rachel would fix them.<br /><br />-Trent and Rachel should have nothing more than a fling. Trent has done too many awful things to Rachel for them to have a believable HEA.<br /><br />-Why was Rachel suddenly acting like she never loved Nick or Pierce? She did love them when they dated. She loved Kisten the most but she definitely loved Nick and Pierce too. <br />Now that Trent's in the picture her love life has been changed — all so what she feels for Trent comes across as speshul and so Trent looks like her 'twu wuv'.<br /><br />-Elves are evil. Why is everyone desperate to save them? They enslaved demons, cursed them so they couldn't breed and then destroyed the paradise that was the ever after because they were pissed that they were no longer controlling the demons. Why are the demons made out to be the bad guys when it's the elves that are bad?!<br /><br />-Also the book was too long.<br /><br /><b>Quotes of interest:</b><br /><br />-<i>Was my life truly this predictable, or did I just keep making the same mistakes over and over?</i><br /><br /><b>Yes, and yes. After 11 books Rachel still hasn't clocked onto the fact that she's an idiot.</b><br /><br />-<i>“I’d be content if I could get an apology for you slamming my head into a tombstone and choking me half to death,”</i> I said.<br />His half smile made something in me twist. <i>“Then I apologize.” <br />“And I accept,” </i>I said, tucking a rank strand of hair back. <i>“It never happened.”</i><br /><br /><b>WHAT!! WTF?! So Trent tortures her for years and tries to kill her and all is forgiven and forgotten after one lame ass apology?!<br />Rachel has no dignity or self respect.</b><br /><br />-<i>“I will never understand you. How can you forgive so easily?”</i><br /><br /><b>Because Rachel is a weak, pathetic doormat that likes being used and abused. If Trent beat her up every night she'd still think he was a decent guy.</b><br /><br />-<i>Why did I always leave such a huge amount of collateral damage?</i><br /><br /><b>Ugh, Rachel is an insufferable martyr and thinks anything bad that happens is all her fault.</b><br /><br />-<i>I thought, wondering how I got to this point: willingly taking the smut for a curse to help Trent.</i><br /><br /><b>Trent doesn't offer to take the smut and he doesn't care about Rachel taking the smut because he's more bothered about himself.</b><br /> <br /><u>Favourite quote</u>:<br /><br />Al to Trent: <i>“Seeing if your circumcision is gone? It is.”</i><br /><br /><br />Al was the only saving grace in the book. Rachel was a doormat. Trent was still a bastard to her and their romance was fucked up.</span>
  <a data-text-id="908711391170071691" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_247452177" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/247452177" />
    <a title="Lynsey   (A Bookish Life)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5112089-lynsey-a-bookish-life"><img alt="Lynsey   (A Bookish Life)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499618776p2/5112089.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/247452177?book_show_action=true">Dec 15, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lynsey   (A Bookish Life)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lynsey   (A Bookish Life)" href="/user/show/5112089-lynsey-a-bookish-life">Lynsey   (A Bookish Life)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5112089-lynsey-a-bookish-life?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5112089-lynsey-a-bookish-life?shelf=received-for-review">received-for-review</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer247452177" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7274685493832031049"><i>
  <b>Kim Harrison is the reigning Queen of Urban Fantasy!</b>
</i><br/><br/>One of the most highly anticipated reads of 2013 for many people, <b>Ever After</b> by Kim Harrison most certainly will not fall short of expectations. It will, in many areas, surpass them. It will also shock, it will thrill, and my goodness it will entertain. An outstanding instalment, easily replacing any and all past favourites as the new pinnacle of the series...so far.<br/><br/>As is usually the case, the story picks up a couple of months after the eve</span>
  <span id="freeText7274685493832031049" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>Kim Harrison is the reigning Queen of Urban Fantasy!</b>
</i><br /><br />One of the most highly anticipated reads of 2013 for many people, <b>Ever After</b> by Kim Harrison most certainly will not fall short of expectations. It will, in many areas, surpass them. It will also shock, it will thrill, and my goodness it will entertain. An outstanding instalment, easily replacing any and all past favourites as the new pinnacle of the series...so far.<br /><br />As is usually the case, the story picks up a couple of months after the events of the last book, <b>A Perfect Blood</b>, and sees Rachel meeting up with Quen to discuss the prospect of becoming a part of Trent's workforce once again. Only voluntarily this time, and will no bodily threats involved. Which makes a nice change. Rachel's not too sure, though, and perhaps not for the reasons you might expect. It seems she puts more faith in Trent's abilities to protect <i>himself</i> than Quen does these days, and doesn't think he needs anyone else watching him. Quite the opposite, in fact. However, after a drastic and heartbreaking turn of events, the choice about working alongside Trent is taken out of her hands completely. It's now imperative, especially since she feels partly responsible for what's happened.<br /><br />Fans of the series will recall Rachel's unfortunate experience with a ley line back in book nine, <b>Pale Demon</b>. For me, personally, those last few chapters of Pale Demon were where my appreciation of Kim Harrison's worldbuilding went from thinking she was simply fabulous, to thinking she might actually be some kind of supernatural creature herself. I mean, she <i>must</i> have been to the Ever After <i>in person</i> to be able to describe it so vividly. And not just visual descriptions, either, but the magic, the culture, the social structure, the history, the wars, the continual decline of the demons as a race. Which, incidentally, Rachel has managed to speed up exponentially by ripping a large hole in one of the ley lines. If only the demons thought it was so incidental. Strangely, they're rather annoyed about their impending doom, and in this book they use one hell of a bargaining chip to make sure Rachel fixes her mistake, and fast. The clock is most definitely ticking.<br /><br />I'm reticent to highlight too many other plot points as I think it's best to just experience it as it unfolds. And it was a real roller coaster, that's for sure. Totally unputdownable with near-perfect pacing. There are some big shocks in store, as I mentioned earlier, some controversial returning characters, plenty of conflict—both internal and external—and a fair amount of introspection for our dear Rache, as well. There were a couple of instances where the plot moved a bit slower, but out of a 500-and-then-some page book, that's really not bad at all. Perhaps even a necessity. Overall, this instalment felt really meaty, with little filler and lots of massive plot twists and character progression that really change the game entirely for the last two books. And of course, being titled <b>Ever After</b>, you can expect to bask in yet more of Harrison's phenomenal worldbuilding for that setting, and also, get some fantastic insight into everyone's favourite demon, Algaliarept. Outstanding stuff!<br /><br />For the Rachel and Trent shippers out there (much like myself) you'll be pleased with the amount of time spent together in this book. Gone are the days where Trent would make one, maybe two, brief appearances—usually managing to annoy the crap out of Rachel in the process—but it's clear now that, in whatever role, Trent is a part of Rachel's life. They make strange bedfellows in some respects, but in other's, they couldn't be more compatible. What's lovely to see as well is the developing trust between them; something we couldn't have ever imagined coming from Rachel even as little as three books ago. It's an amazing transformation and a fantastic journey Kim Harrison has taken us on. I'm sad to think there's just two teeny weeny little books left in this series, but judging by the ending of this book, they're gonna be good ones! Oh, yeah.<br /><br />5 Stars ★★★★★<br />A special thanks to Harper Voyager for the ARC. I read many ARCs throughout the year, but to receive one for your favourite series is a special treat. Like Christmas come early!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7274685493832031049" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_450125794" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/450125794" />
    <a title="Jen Davis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4669344-jen-davis"><img alt="Jen Davis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548427639p2/4669344.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/450125794?book_show_action=true">Nov 06, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jen Davis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jen Davis" href="/user/show/4669344-jen-davis">Jen Davis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4669344-jen-davis?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer450125794" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4437182413523868266">This is my absolute favorite installment of the Hollows series to date. The best book I have read in months. I loved it. Loved it. Loved it. Loved it. It's as though Kim Harrison made this book to order, handpicking all of my favorite elements of the series and letting them shine. Tons of Trent. Al. Jenks. And, of course, the ever after. It's light on Ivy, the vampire culture, witches and werewolves. And we actually see real growth in Rachel. It's like Christmas and my birthday all at once.<br/><br/>The s</span>
  <span id="freeText4437182413523868266" style="display:none">This is my absolute favorite installment of the Hollows series to date. The best book I have read in months. I loved it. Loved it. Loved it. Loved it. It's as though Kim Harrison made this book to order, handpicking all of my favorite elements of the series and letting them shine. Tons of Trent. Al. Jenks. And, of course, the ever after. It's light on Ivy, the vampire culture, witches and werewolves. And we actually see real growth in Rachel. It's like Christmas and my birthday all at once.<br /><br />The story feels more like a follow up to Pale Demon than A Perfect Blood. We're experiencing a lot of repercussions from that book. The ley line Rachel accidentally made is leaking --and slowly destroying the ever after. Of course, she is blamed, but it's really Ku'Sox who is setting her up. He exacerbated the problems with the lines to put Rachel in the crosshairs --and he'll only fix the problem if she takes the curse off of him that keeps him away from her reality.<br /><br />Ku'Sox is also gunning for Trent. He's been kidnapping Rosewood babies and he wants Trent to manipulate their genes to make more day-walking demons like Rachel. Ku'Sox wants control of the babies to boost his power among the demons. Trent won't budge, so Ku'Sox takes desperate action. Trent and Rachel must work together to best Ku'Sox, as the demon endangers those near and dear to both of their hearts... and all of demonkind.<br /><br />There is a ton of action in this book. I was pulled in from the very beginning and I did not want to put it down until the last page. It is unpredictable. Remember the kind of shockers Kim Harrison delivered in some of the earlier books in the series? Oh yeah, those are back. At right about the halfway mark, she kicked me in the gut --hard. No punches are pulled. No easy roads are taken. It had me by the seat of my pants the whole time.<br /><br />One of the things I love about these books is the continuity. Harrison never tries to ignore past events. Instead, she weaves them into current stories, reminding us of those things that built the characters into who they are. From the rat fights to the doctor Trent killed --from Rachel's failed romances to Denon's death and the boat explosion. It's all there and then some... all kinds of little Easter Eggs for longtime fans.<br /><br />We continue to learn more about the demons --and their history. We meet more gargoyles. Learn more about the ever after. Plot Ellsbeth's death (wait... maybe that last part was just me.) And we get movement on the whole Rachel and Trent will-they or won't-they dance. I won't spoil it. But it's a pretty big story thread, or at least, a major current throughout the book.<br /><br />I am forcing myself to stop gushing now, before I tell you everything that happened. Just know that if you were on the fence about continuing this series after A Perfect Blood, please take my advice and read this book. If it doesn't make you fall in love with The Hollows again, I don't know what will.<br /><br />Rating: A<br /><br /><i>*ARC Provided by Harper Collins</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="4437182413523868266" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15608824850668441419"><blockquote>
  <b>“My God, you have beautiful hair in the firelight,” he said softly, and I blinked. “It’s like your thoughts, all cinnamon and wild untamed. I’ve always liked your hair.”</b>
</blockquote><br/><br/> ~ sigh ~ <br/><br/>For those of us who have anxiously awaited each Hollows book, we <u>knew</u> the moment Trenton Aloysius Kalamack came on the scene that he was the one for Rachel! And what's funny is this is NOT a romance book. It is very much an Urban Fantasy! (Lord help us if KH ever decides to write a romance.) <br/><br/>Trent has not been nice </span>
  <span id="freeText15608824850668441419" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>“My God, you have beautiful hair in the firelight,” he said softly, and I blinked. “It’s like your thoughts, all cinnamon and wild untamed. I’ve always liked your hair.”</b>
</blockquote><br /><br /> ~ sigh ~ <br /><br />For those of us who have anxiously awaited each Hollows book, we <u>knew</u> the moment Trenton Aloysius Kalamack came on the scene that he was the one for Rachel! And what's funny is this is NOT a romance book. It is very much an Urban Fantasy! (Lord help us if KH ever decides to write a romance.) <br /><br />Trent has not been nice to Rachel, in fact, he has been very mean and Rachel, by trying to be a better person, is determined not to forget that. The problem is that Rachel can't help but remember the good in people and that colors her view. It also has made her start to fall for Trent. Would I be happy with nothing but a Trent and Rachel romance? Well, a girl can dream right? But...let me get to the rest of the story because as much as I love Rachel and Trent, The Hollows stories are so much more!<br /><br />Rachel's ley line that she created has been causing problems and for some reason, it is eating up more space in the ever after. Al goes with her to see if they can determine what the problem is and they find out that Ku'Sox is behind it. Rachel also realizes that he is behind the missing Rosewood syndrome babies and that Nick (!!) is helping him. <br /><br />This book is full of action and has a lot of things going on. Some things were quite surprising, unsettling and....almost unbelievable. KH pulls no punches and things get serious rather quickly...for Rachel as well as several other characters. You can also see that KH is starting to wrap up several story lines - even if they are somewhat unexpected.<br /><br />For the most part, I liked how things went. There are some emotional, angsty parts but there are also some sweet, heartwarming scenes. We get more information about Al and demons in general and more information on Trent's elven powers. I enjoyed seeing more depth to these two characters. They've been with us for a long time and while they were intended to be the bad guys, it is great seeing them come together and work for the greater good. <br /><br />The rest of the crew is around and involved...Jenks, Ivy, Pierce, and even Jax, just to name a few. I liked how she updated us with the characters and even reminisced a bit. It was great hearing about some of their prior events...almost like a walk down memory lane. And the rings? I loved what they did and what they brought out in the characters. What a wonderful addition to the story! <br /><br />Steamy sex scenes? Well, of course, there are none but like I said KH does know how to do romance. I'm sure it didn't hurt that I read romance into every Trent word and gesture but seriously, the cookie maker has some moves! <br /><br />I can't really go into much without giving this away. Suffice to say, I think if you're current with this series, you will not be disappointed...and what an ending!! I LOVED IT! Unfortunately, we have to wait a year for the next one. <br /><br /><br />Favorite quotes: <br /><br />♥ "Feeling two orgasms at once might be worth the invasion of privacy."<br /><br />♦ "I like it, fairy woman! I'm wearing it!"<br /><br />♥ “I want,” he said softly, “you to keep what you can of the person you want to be. Don’t sacrifice it for this.”<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15608824850668441419" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10452133358711377421">Updated review:<br/><br/>Now that I have some time, I need to rip open a few assholes. <br/><br/>TRENT: Fuck him and Quen and ALL the elves.   <span id="freeText10452133358711377421" style="display:none">Updated review:<br /><br />Now that I have some time, I need to rip open a few assholes. <br /><br />TRENT: Fuck him and Quen and ALL the elves. If they are the representatives of the race, then mother fuck them. Don't worry, Rachel doesn't feel the same way. It's all aces 10 and good vibes and hackey sacks and shit. I won't tell you what happens, but I consider it a betrayal BEYOND even when Trent locked her up and put her in the rat fights. For a while I thought Rachel was royally fucked. Another huge manipulation by Trent and Quen happened. Even though Trent apologized, it is unforgivable. I've NEVER been on the Trent and Rachel bandwagon. It feels nasty to me. Like going back to an abuser or something. Also, Trent can BE whatever he wants and still save the elven race. I don't see the big deal. I'm a little tired that. <br /><br />CERI: Who the fuck does she think she is. This isn't 1000 years ago or whatever sweety. You are no longer royalty. Did you forget that if not for Rachel, you would still be Al's vacant, slightly insane blow up doll? Why are you so uppity and being bitchy to Rachel for not helping Trent. It's up to HER and she owes YOU and HIM nothing. In fact you should be lying prostrate at her feet every time you see her! I am not sorry....<br /><br />Elf Babies: OMG, they were so adorable, but what's with the weird parental shit. Yes, I know that for public purposes little Ray is being presented as Trent and Ceri's child. Sometimes it feels weird when she kisses him on the cheek or something. WTF? <br /><br />Ivy: She's out of town more most of it and comes back to help Rachel do a run. She's interested in Nina, who is of course fucked up...and of course that get Rachel caught up psycho vampire shit. I like Ivy, but for the first time, in this book, I found myself irritated. Why do the vampires exist? They are all so morbid and emo. I'm sick of the controlling master vampires and the unhealthy relationships and people having to tip-toe around them because they can't control themselves! Fuck the vampires! <br /><br />Rachel: Oh, Rachel. How fond of you I am, but you need to figure out what you want and don't settle for less. Stop saying sorry all the time. Kick even more ass with demon magic. Stop worrying about the smut on your soul. Stop trusting Trent, he doesn't deserve it. Trent has you on speed dial for when dangerous bullshit comes up. Quen shows up and makes ridiculous demands on you and you ALWAYS give in. Just fucking stop it. I think Al loves you or could. He's certainly the only candidate on the field as far as I'm concerned. <br /><br /><br /><br /><br />original review below.....................................................<br /><br /><br />That was AMAZING! That crazy bastard has not only taken them, but has cursed the Rachel's leaking leyline so that it is literally destroying and shrinking the Ever After. That's not even the half of it. <br /><br />There wasn't one dull moment in the story. It was constant anxiety as lives, magic, creatures, and more on the brink of total destruction. <br /><br />Ku'sox was diabolical and very fun to hate. He really took the psycho up to another level. I love Al so much. We got to spend lots of time with him and several other demons in the Ever After, which I missed from the last book. <br /><br />Tentative alliances are formed, beloved or maybe not so beloved characters show up, lives are destroyed, elf babies are ADORABLE, bitches get put in their place etc etc etc. <br /><br />Fans of the series will not be disappointed. It likes The Hollows on steroids, with past story lines and our favorite characters at their best and worst. The magic of it all wrapped around me like a cozy blanket and I can't wait to visit the story again...and again. <br /><br />Will there be more? Oooo, that ending was... </span>
  <a data-text-id="10452133358711377421" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_421016656" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/421016656" />
    <a title="Lyndi W." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5913818-lyndi-w"><img alt="Lyndi W." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1494401300p2/5913818.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/421016656?book_show_action=true">Sep 24, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lyndi W." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lyndi W." href="/user/show/5913818-lyndi-w">Lyndi W.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5913818-lyndi-w?shelf=3-star">3-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer421016656" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6784766206031837597">I'm having trouble with this series. I loved the beginning, but I'm getting a little tired of it now. The writing is fine, the characters are fine, but the plot... Jesus! It's just constant, never-ending grade-A <i>bad shit</i> happening to Rachel. Every single book. The odds are stacked against her, yes yes we get that. But how much shit can you pile onto a character before it just gets ridiculous? I'm thinking about 10 books worth, because this 11th was downright annoying.<br/><br/>Everyone's trying to kill he</span>
  <span id="freeText6784766206031837597" style="display:none">I'm having trouble with this series. I loved the beginning, but I'm getting a little tired of it now. The writing is fine, the characters are fine, but the plot... Jesus! It's just constant, never-ending grade-A <i>bad shit</i> happening to Rachel. Every single book. The odds are stacked against her, yes yes we get that. But how much shit can you pile onto a character before it just gets ridiculous? I'm thinking about 10 books worth, because this 11th was downright annoying.<br /><br />Everyone's trying to kill her. Everyone is lying to her. Everyone blames her. I mean, can a bitch get a break? Apparently not.<br /><br />And this is seriously the largest cast of characters ever - how am I supposed to keep track of them? I guess I don't, since Kim Harrison keeps killing them off. And it's never the right one. She took Faulkner's "kill your darlings" quote to heart, that's for damn sure. I won't mention <b>who</b> dies, but just be warned that it's <i>not</i> who you want to die. I'm pretty sure we all wanted this particular character to die like... 10 books ago, but the author just won't give us that satisfaction. Nope. Instead, she kills off the people we love, like Kisten.<br /><br />I don't know how I feel about this series anymore. Ask me at book 9, I would have said it's one of my top 5 favorite series. But with the author killing off all the people I like, dragging out the romantic pairing foreeeeveeerrrrr, and the shovels upon shovels of shit that she keeps dumping on Rachel... I'm losing my patience. I'm never glad when a series ends, but I may just celebrate the ending of this one. If Rachel can't get her HEA after 12 books, the bitch doesn't deserve it.<br /><br />Although now I'm half expecting the author to kill off Rachel before the end of it. Just to break all our hearts. She seems to enjoy doing that. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6784766206031837597" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5693840-shenanigans?shelf=witchy-business">witchy-business</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5693840-shenanigans?shelf=ass-kicking-heroine">ass-kicking-heroine</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer390662195" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3844350632595221167">*Spoilage*<br/>***Three 1/2 Stars!***<br/><br/>For me, three stars for Ever After is generous. I am a bit let down and disappointed in this book. Although I do not recommend anyone skip this book if they plan on reading anymore of this series. A few things happen that will surely have you lost with the next book if you skip this one. So. Read this shit.<br/><br/>From the opening paragraph, something about this felt different to me. Rachel seemed off, a touch more wordy and emotional than she'd been in the last book, A P</span>
  <span id="freeText3844350632595221167" style="display:none">*Spoilage*<br />***Three 1/2 Stars!***<br /><br />For me, three stars for Ever After is generous. I am a bit let down and disappointed in this book. Although I do not recommend anyone skip this book if they plan on reading anymore of this series. A few things happen that will surely have you lost with the next book if you skip this one. So. Read this shit.<br /><br />From the opening paragraph, something about this felt different to me. Rachel seemed off, a touch more wordy and emotional than she'd been in the last book, A Perfect Blood. I overlooked it. Then things kept being mentioned, events that apparently had happened in past books, people I remembered almost nothing about and major plot points I felt had no place in this book kept popping up. I was con-freaking-fused for a great deal of it but still, I credited it to me not having read any of the past Hollows books in a while; I was just a little misty on the past details. <br /><br />Ku'Sox reprised his role in Ever After, making big waves and causing <i>poor</i> Trenton HUGE problems. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Kidnapping his daughter and her Stand-In mommy made the big bad Elf vewy angwy. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Nick and a few other almost-forgotten characters also popped in to say heylo, too.<br /><br />Al seemed a little less snarky than usual, the snap and bite gone from his words. Jenks...ahh, he was still Jenks, I suppose. Just not...<i>Jenks</i>. I wish I could explain it better, but I can't. Ivy was absent for almost all of this book, hopping in for the last seven or so chapters but playing as small a role as Harrison dared without cutting her out of the book entirely. Which <i>
  <b>vexed</b>
</i> me greatly. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[And she fucking killed Ceri!! <b>BY TINK'S LITTLE PINK NIPPLES, WHY WOULD YOU DO THAT?!</b>  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />*Breathes deeply* Okay. I'm sorry for snapping. I just...It was stupid. And I was enjoying the book up until then. First Piscary, Kisten, Matalina, and NOW <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Ceri and Pierce - who was technically already dead but you catch my drift. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Obviously Harrison has no qualms about killing off her characters. As quiet as kept, I like her all the better for it. I love a good ballsy author who isn't afraid to kill off a few people. Keeps things lively.<br /><br />Trenton was a bit too mushy-romance-y for comfort, IMO anyway. It seemed to be a bit out of character for him but then again...this book kinda flip flopped around. Everybody felt a little disjointed. To me at least. Al....gosh. Rachel didn't get slapped or hit on by him once in this entire book. <b>NOT. ONCE.</b> I didn't get it. By all rights, Al should be such a pig, I'm forced to find him nothing but dangerously, wittingly charming in a weird sort of I'm-So-Obtuse-And-Offensive-With-My-Completely-Garish-Flirting-That-I've-Looped-Back-Over-To-Sexy kind of way.<br /><br />Hey, don't judge me. Al is badass.<br /><br />Rachel's favorite new word was Sorry. She said it to every single person besides herself in the damn book. If I never ever read the word 'Sorry' coming from Rachel's mouth again, it'll be too soon. Rachel seemed to break off her tough-ass-kicking-demon self and flush it down the toilet before this book because not an ounce of her HAPA and Coven ass kicking self was shown on a single page of this book. Nick was able to get the drop on her and give her a good smack. <i>Nick.</i> Does no one else see the problem with this? Alas, I was disappointed. <br /><br />Ellasbeth gave me a good giggle, though. Man, she is just awful. But I love her as a character.<br /><br />The whole big-bad/antagonist/oh-shit-we've-got-trouble factor in this book was reallyyyy good. The whole <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Rosewood baby kidnapping <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> thing - friggin <b>GENIUS</b>. But I feel it was played all wrong. Harrison could've taken it to unforeseen heights, built a platform/big-bad for the next book kind of branching off this, but it just didn't do it. I kind of feel like she's setting things up to pull Ivy completely from the series and leave Rachel with just Jenks and a handful of his kids. Oh, and Belle. Can't forget the Fairy. But, no more Ivy? Is she INSANE?!<br /><br />ALTHOUGH, I <i>DO</i> feel like that ending with Trent just might have made <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Ceri's death <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> tolerable. Maybe.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3844350632595221167" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_286291300" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/286291300" />
    <a title="Catie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1886642-catie"><img alt="Catie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1385169623p2/1886642.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/286291300?book_show_action=true">Feb 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Catie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Catie" href="/user/show/1886642-catie">Catie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=lgbtqia">lgbtqia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=read-in-2013">read-in-2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer286291300" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15199269238239610579">The Hollows are back…and so am I! (I hope.) What better way to kick off my reviewing dust than to write about a series I’ve loved for almost a decade? Even though I was mostly disappointed last January by the slow-moving rehash of old events that was <i>A Perfect Blood</i>, I knew that this author wouldn’t hold still for long. This series, which now encompasses eleven books and will end at book thirteen (Thanks Megan!) never ceases to be inventive and surprising.<br/><br/>This book sees Rachel & Co. moving forwa</span>
  <span id="freeText15199269238239610579" style="display:none">The Hollows are back…and so am I! (I hope.) What better way to kick off my reviewing dust than to write about a series I’ve loved for almost a decade? Even though I was mostly disappointed last January by the slow-moving rehash of old events that was <i>A Perfect Blood</i>, I knew that this author wouldn’t hold still for long. This series, which now encompasses eleven books and will end at book thirteen (Thanks Megan!) never ceases to be inventive and surprising.<br /><br />This book sees Rachel &amp; Co. moving forward once again. Trouble is afoot in the ever after as Ceri and baby Lucy are kidnapped in the opening chapters and Rachel’s ley line suddenly starts draining the ever after at an alarming rate. The demons find it more convenient to blame Rachel, even though they all know that lab-created demon monstrosity Ku’Sox (aka Cute Socks) is to blame. In an effort to save the day for everyone once again, Rachel finds herself working more closely with Trent and the elves than she ever has before.<br /><br />This is the installment that the Rachel/Trent fans have been waiting for. Harrison has been flirting with the idea of them as a couple for quite a while, and in this book I felt like she finally jumped off that cliff. I’m still not sure if I will be able to buy into their relationship as a long term thing. Harrison has certainly laid a lot of ground work over the past books, but a huge part of me will probably never be able to stop seeing Trent as the spoiled, arrogant rich pretty boy he was in the first book. (He also made a comment at the end of this book that really turned me off. It's pretty spoilery but I'll discuss in the comments if anyone's interested.) <br /><br />However, it’s refreshing to look back and realize just how much he (and Al and Rachel and Ivy and well…everyone) has changed. This series never stagnates for me because Harrison lets her characters grow. After reading this book, I now feel like while <i>A Perfect Blood</i> may have been slow and tedious to read; it was ultimately a necessary step in the series. Rachel is more at home with her demon identity than ever, and it’s exciting to see her finally accept and use her powers to their fullest extent, without endless angst about the consequences. Harrison grows her characters slowly but surely – in short, realistically. Perhaps that means that one or two of these books has been more like a “transition” book but I think the end result is a much more fulfilling, believable story. I have faith that she'll make me believe in Trent by book thirteen.<br /><br />(As an aside – Harrison’s short story, <i>Trouble on Reserve</i>, <a href="https://play.google.com/store/apps/details?id=com.sony.drbd.tablet.reader.other.usca&amp;feature=nav_result#?t=W10" rel="nofollow noopener">available for free with download of the Sony Reader App</a> – went a long way toward convincing me of Trent’s worthiness and feelings for Rachel.)<br /><br />As an extra today, I’d like to pay homage to <a href="http://www.thereadventurer.com/1/post/2012/08/50-things-guaranteed-to-happen-in-an-installment-of-jd-robbs-in-death-series.html" rel="nofollow noopener">one of my favorite posts of Flannery’s</a> by listing “50 things very nearly guaranteed to happen” in a Hollows book. Like Flannery, I write these very much in good humor as a super-fan of Kim Harrison and her Hollows books. Yes, there is a certain formula to these books but what impresses me the most is how much Harrison frequently tosses that formula out the window.<br /><br />Head over to <a href="http://www.thereadventurer.com/1/post/2013/02/adult-review-ever-after-by-kim-harrison.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Readventurer</a> to read my list.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15199269238239610579" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_286307317" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/286307317" />
    <a title="AH" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3255548-ah"><img alt="AH" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1275413869p2/3255548.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/286307317?book_show_action=true">Feb 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="AH" class="user" itemprop="url" name="AH" href="/user/show/3255548-ah">AH</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=demons">demons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=ghosts">ghosts</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=arc-edelweiss">arc-edelweiss</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=zzread-dec-2012">zzread-dec-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=were">were</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=witches">witches</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer286307317" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10152432755670555494">5 stars for another fantastic installment in the Hollows series. <br/><br/>I’ve loved The Hollows since I discovered the series a few years ago. I’ve stood by and watched Rachel grow and change over the course of the series. I can honestly say that this is the best book so far in the series – and I hear that there are still two more books to go. <br/><br/>I think what makes this series so good is its evolution of the main characters, especially that of Rachel Morgan. Rachel’s growth, her maturity, her change into a</span>
  <span id="freeText10152432755670555494" style="display:none">5 stars for another fantastic installment in the Hollows series. <br /><br />I’ve loved The Hollows since I discovered the series a few years ago. I’ve stood by and watched Rachel grow and change over the course of the series. I can honestly say that this is the best book so far in the series – and I hear that there are still two more books to go. <br /><br />I think what makes this series so good is its evolution of the main characters, especially that of Rachel Morgan. Rachel’s growth, her maturity, her change into a strong, kickass heroine (as opposed to the loose cannon she was in earlier books) is what makes this series one of my favorites. Of course, it helps to surround Rachel with a diverse group of eccentric, talented, loyal, and trash-talking secondary characters. <br /><br />This book feels like a study of Rachel’s relationships. Not just romantic relationships, although I’d love to see more of that – and note to Ms. Harrison – please stop killing off Rachel’s lovers! <b>Ever After</b> is a study of Rachel’s relationships with the world around her, be it The Hollows or the <b>Ever After</b>. <br /><br />Rachel and Trent are spending more time together. Mostly business, but a girl can hope, right? We’d love to see more because these two work so well together. Clearly, the two are attracted to each other, but Rachel have some reservations about Trent. <br /><br />We learn a lot about the history of the demons and elves and why they are constantly at odds with each other. It only goes to show that grudges in this world can last for a very long time. I loved the fascinating bits about the magical rings. A touch of Lord of the Rings, Hollows-style. <br /><br />Rachel and Al’s relationship has evolved, too. I don’t see them as student-teacher any more, but more as equals as Rachel’s magical abilities improve. Rachel has also become quite well versed in demon politics, thanks to Al. Whereas in the past, she may have just mouthed off, she now takes the time to carefully weigh and word her requests and she ensures that she has been understood correctly. I would have never imagined Rachel of the earlier books being able to do this. <br /><br />I’ve always loved the secondary characters in this series. The demons were always a source of entertainment for me – I enjoyed watching just how they planned to screw things up for Rachel and each other. Newt the crazy demon had a touching moment where she helped Rachel choose an outfit to save the world in. <br /><br />No discussion of this series can be complete without talking about Ivy and Jenks. Lately, I’ve had enough of Ivy and I was kind of glad that she isn’t really in this book as a main character. She’s off doing her own thing for most of the book and that was OK with me. Jenks, on the other hand, with his little comments about Tink always brings comic relief to a tense situation. My heart broke for him as he worried about his estranged son Jax. I was so happy that he had Belle around to take care of him. <br /><br />I also loved how a certain innocuous character suddenly became a superstar in this book. I always saw Bis as a little gargoyle, attracted to Rachel. I’m so glad we learned more about the gargoyles in this book. <br /><br />The Hollows series is one of my favorite urban fantasy series. In my opinion, <b>Ever After</b> is the best book in the series so far. More, please!<br /><br /><i> Thank you to Edelweiss and Harper Voyager for a review copy of this book.</i><br /><br /><b>Check out our group discussion of Ever After on <a href="http://badassbookreviews.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Badass Book Reviews.</a></b><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10152432755670555494" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2870845634464139429"><b>Re-read July 2015</b><br/><br/>Everything has been said already. I'm just as blown away as the first time I read this book, and I still can't believe some of the things Kim did to those characters. Whyyyy you so evil? *wails* <br/><br/>Saying I loved it, heartbreak and all, is putting it mildly.   <span id="freeText2870845634464139429" style="display:none"><b>Re-read July 2015</b><br /><br />Everything has been said already. I'm just as blown away as the first time I read this book, and I still can't believe some of the things Kim did to those characters. Whyyyy you so evil? *wails* <br /><br />Saying I loved it, heartbreak and all, is putting it mildly. This one was one of the most complex, different, action packed and emotional books in the series, and it let me a happy reader, but slightly scarred, heartbroken and hangover, so I'm going to take a short break before I read the <u>last</u> two books - which I haven't read <u>at all</u> yet. I'm scared and procrastinating LOL. I need recovery time before I can deal with that. I'd say I love Al and Trent, and that final battle was beyond epic, but that'd the understatement of the year. So... I'm just going to leave a few of my favorite quotes here and go process it all. <br /><br /><br /><i>Though I’d seen both men take down an attacker, Quen would always use the minimal amount of force, whereas Trent would be a conflict of visions—elegance coupled with savagery and a frightening grace, magic sung into existence.</i><br />***<br /><br /><i>“Al!” I cried out, hand outstretched.<br />Al stopped, turned, and gave me a last look. Hold on to me, I saw him say, hearing it echo in my thoughts as well. Don’t let go. <br />And then, he stepped into the purple line.</i><br />***<br /><br /><i>“Ivy, I’m cold. Jenks is cold. As soon as Jax gets off that gargoyle’s hand, he’s going to be cold. Nick is strapped and the risk is minimal. Can we please go inside? I have to save the world tomorrow, and I don’t even know what I’m going to wear yet.” </i><br />***<br /><br /><i>Illegal. Everything we were doing was illegal, and not for the first time, I wondered how I’d gotten to this place, doing illegal things to help Trent. Help him save the world.</i><br />***<br /><br /><i>“I like people. Most of the time I can figure them out. You don’t make any sense. What are you looking for, Rachel?” <br />Drawing my knees up, I rocked back and forth before the fire. “I don’t know. Someone smart, powerful, who doesn’t take crap from anyone. Who are you looking for?” (...)<br />“Someone funny, capable, sexy.” <br />To balance out his strict life. “I didn’t bring looks into it. How like a man.”</i><br /><br />_________________________<br /><br />**First read: 2013**<br /><br />Wow. Just... wow. I still can't believe half of the things that happened in this book and the way they happened. What an action-packed, emotional, shocking, amazing ride! It was almost like reading Shadowfever all over again - and it's probably one of the best (if no THE best) UF books I've read since that one. I need to sort through my thoughts and my emotions (which are all over the place right now), but OMG I LOVED, LOVED, LOVED IT! Every second of it... Even through the heartbreak. :'( Definitely my favorite book of the series. ♥ Oh, and Trent... *sigh* There are no words right now. ♥<br /><br />~6 glowing stars</span>
